"May Day" Demonstrations in Germany and Russia; Voroshilov Says Strength Sufficient to Destroy Enemy; Hitler Announces Desire for Peace 39

(Moscow) Yesterday's May Day commemoration was the largest demonstration in the 18 years since the founding of Soviet Russia, and it was full of ridicule for capitalist countries, especially Japan and Germany. The Red Army held a parade in Red Square, and 650 large bombers circled in the air. More than one million civilians participated in the parade. The flags and slogans held by the parading masses were all words ridiculing the people of other countries. Soviet Minister of War Voroshilov said in a speech after inspecting the troops, "If anyone forces us to fight, then these people will experience the strength of our army." U.S. Ambassador Bullitt also participated in the parade. A 72-foot-tall giant statue of Stalin was hung on the front of the building in front of the square. During the parade, the people cheered for Stalin. This inspection was sufficient to show the rapid progress of the Soviet army in recent months. (National News Agency, 2nd)

(Berlin) "We are telling the people of all countries in the world that the Germans want nothing from the world. We do not want war, we only want world peace. But the Germans will never give up their honor." This is the National Socialist Party's policy platform proclaimed by German leader Hitler in two speeches to the general public in Berlin yesterday on National Day. Hitler's speech to 600,000 people at Tempelhof Airport was extremely short, lasting only 26 minutes. (National News Agency, 2nd)

(Berlin) Today is Germany's National Labor Day. The weather is cold and snowing. Hundreds of thousands of employers and workers gathered in the snow at the Lustgarten to celebrate. German leader Hitler, suffering from a sore throat, gave only a brief speech, saying that Germany's ambition is for peace. The international political situation is full of thorns, and only by enduring hardship can the struggling German people overcome major difficulties. May 1st is the day our nation makes a decision. We must be determined, united, and inseparable. (Havas, 1st)

(Berlin) Yesterday was Germany's National Labor Day. Aviation Minister and Prussian Governor General Goering gave a speech in the Lustgarten, saying that Germany is like an anvil, being hammered by others. It cannot endure this any longer. From now on, Germany's peace will no longer be controlled by the political forces of other countries. Our new military formations have been organized. Our national flag can now fly at sea. Our air security is guaranteed by aircraft squadrons. At this time, those who are in charge of national affairs are no longer weaklings, but brave men. Germany can now rest easy. You must remember that Germany's revival depends entirely on the victory of the leader Hitler. (Havas, 2nd)

General Situation of May First in Various Countries 40

(London) Although today is Labor Day in the world's major capitals, most are peaceful and uneventful. However, a bomb exploded in the Austrian capital, seriously injuring four or five people. The authorities are strictly arresting communists and have detained 500 people. Last night, a bomb exploded outside a police station in the suburbs of Vienna, injuring four passersby with shrapnel. They have been sent to the hospital. As a result, the authorities took the major action of arresting communists today. Most capitals have made advance preparations to prevent disturbances. Apart from minor clashes, this Labor Day has passed peacefully. More than one million people gathered at an airfield in Berlin, where Hitler gave a speech, saying, "We do not want war. We want world peace, just as we want to restore domestic peace." In Paris, both the Communist Party and the Socialist Party held meetings in Villette. The authorities did not allow them to hold open-air gatherings. The military police were prepared to defend, and the authorities also used airplanes to patrol various places to see if there were any illegal gatherings. A very large demonstration was held in Moscow, with 650 of the latest aircraft circling in the sky. Enlarged photos of Stalin were hung on the highest buildings in the city, some as long as 72 feet. All over Germany, Labor Day was celebrated, but the weather was uncertain, with sunshine at times and heavy snow at others. Propaganda Minister Goebbels spoke first at the meeting, saying, "We all know that the purpose of the army is to protect our work. This kind of protection is better than the Treaty of Versailles." Hitler only spoke for a few minutes due to a sore throat. In Marseille, all boats and vehicles were stopped today. Ships that were originally scheduled to sail today have been postponed until tomorrow because dockers and sailors have stopped working. Municipal workers have also stopped working. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

(Paris) The world is gradually moving away from the threat of May Day. Statistics show that more than ten people died and dozens were injured in various countries, and hundreds were arrested. In Iminovo village, Bulgaria, three policemen and five communists died. According to current news, the area is indeed the most eventful center of May Day. According to unofficial reports, the Communist Party intended to hold a meeting in the village after interfering with dance parties of nearby farmers and merchants, resulting in a conflict. After midnight, a riot broke out in the Bagneux area near Paris, killing one gendarme and seriously injuring 28 civilians. Police and rioters chased each other for an hour. The police initially planned to suppress the crowd peacefully, but after one policeman was killed by communists, they opened fire. The two sides clashed for an hour, and the communists were dispersed. More than 50 handguns and bayonets were seized. New York always experiences riots on May Day. Although there was a large-scale demonstration this time, no incidents occurred. 1,600 policemen in the city were dispatched by order of the mayor to prevent disturbances. A bomb exploded in Breitenlee, Vienna, injuring four people. The entire city was ordered to prevent disturbances, and police rushed to the scene. More than 400 people were arrested, including 150 who resisted the police when they were detained. There was also a group of National Socialists who drove through the working-class district, distributing leaflets, attacking Chancellor Schuschnigg and denouncing his government as dishonorable. A telegram from the capital of Romania stated that 18 communists were arrested for plotting to set up obstacles in the streets and seize public buildings. Although Paris is a nest of communists, no serious incidents occurred, only the assassination of one policeman. A May Day demonstration was held in Tokyo, but there were no signs of instability. The participants were mostly left-wing and right-wing workers in the labor movement. (National Telegram, 2nd)

Moscow: A military parade was held at Red Square at 10 a.m. today. The Moscow garrison, armed workers, members of the Young Communist League, student groups, and guerrillas who had previously participated in the civil war participated in the parade. People's Commissar of Defense Voroshilov served as the inspector. The ceremony began with a solemn oath taken by young Red Army soldiers, followed by a speech by Voroshilov. Magnificent artillery, cavalry, infantry, and mechanized units, as well as large and small tank units, paraded across Red Square in perfect order. At the same time, numerous bombers, fighters, reconnaissance aircraft, and other aircraft soared in the sky. Before the parade began, Stalin, Molotov, Kaganovich, Kalinin, and other members of the Politburo and government ascended the Lenin Mausoleum rostrum. Thunderous applause greeted them from below. Foreign diplomats, military attachés, and foreign workers' delegations were also present. After the parade, workers, officials, scientists, and artists from Moscow held a large-scale procession, carrying banners and slogans as they marched through Red Square, showcasing the achievements of various factories, regions, and islands, as well as the successes in various aspects of Soviet life and construction. The streets of Moscow were filled with workers celebrating May Day, and revolutionary songs echoed through the sky, with unparalleled enthusiasm. Major Soviet cities such as Leningrad, Kyiv, Minsk, Tashkent, Khabarovsk, and Tbilisi also held grand parades and processions. (TASS dispatch, 1st)

Vienna: A military parade was held today to commemorate May Day. A service was held at St. Stephen's Cathedral at 8 a.m. this morning, attended by the President and cabinet members. At 9:45 a.m., a large-scale children's rally was held at the sports field, and President Miklas attended and gave a speech. At noon, workers' representatives and professional groups warmly welcomed Chancellor Schuschnigg. The Chancellor was then hosted by the Mayor at the City Hall. In the evening, the dance halls, palaces, Heroes' Memorial, and other famous buildings in the city were brightly lit. All cinemas provided free admission to unemployed workers. (National Telegram, 1st)

Paris: Today is International Labor Day. The Communist Party and the Socialist Party held demonstrations as usual. However, according to the latest news, the whole city is completely safe and sound. Vehicles on the street travel as usual, and only a part of the construction workers are on strike. (Havas dispatch, 1st)

(Paris) Although the Communist Party and the Socialist Party tried their best to hold demonstrations that would cause class warfare on May Day, all major cities in France have passed peacefully without causing serious incidents. Public passenger and freight vehicles operate as usual, and even the most communist-colored car drivers are still on duty. Paris is full of the joyful atmosphere of May Day. Thousands of florists sell flowers as usual, and cafes and taverns are open all day. However, workers in the construction industry took a day off. About 2,000 members of the Socialist Party and the Communist Party held an open-air gathering in front of the Ministry of Labor, passing a resolution demanding that the government adopt an active plan to relieve unemployed workers and enforce a 40-hour work week. The Socialist Party also called for the conclusion of an international agreement based on the unity of all parties to prevent aggression. The Socialist Party also paraded in Lille, Marseille, and several industrial centers, but no disputes arose. (National Telegram, 1st)

New York: The American May Day Labor Day passed peacefully. Although there was a large-scale demonstration in New York City, which has been rare for many years, the order was good. 18,000 police officers were on hand to monitor without interference. One million members of the Socialist Party and 50,000 members of the Communist Party participated in two demonstrations, holding small flags and denouncing imperialist wars, President Roosevelt, and Senator Long, and others. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

Tokyo: The Japanese labor class held the 16th Labor Day today. The General Federation of Labor, the Social Democratic Party, the Japan Labor Union, and other factions held a meeting in a certain park. The Tokyo Transportation Labor Union, the Kanto Labor Union, and other groups held meetings in Shibaura, and then each group paraded through the streets. More than 10,000 people participated. (Japanese United Press dispatch, 1st)

(Tokyo) Today is the 16th Labor Day. The left and right factions of the labor movement are still opposed to each other, so they marched separately. Four thousand members from seven groups under the right-wing Japan General Federation of Labor, chaired by Tokunaga Masahō of the General Federation, departed from Shiba Park, the gathering place, at 11 a.m., singing labor songs, and began marching towards Ueno Park. About 3,000 members from 13 groups under the left-wing Tokyo Transportation Labor Union Council, led by Nohira Suematsu, chairman of the Tokyo Transportation Committee, marched from the reclaimed land of Shibatakashita-cho to Ueno at 1 p.m. The final dispersal time was 4 p.m. The Metropolitan Police Department dispatched about 3,000 uniformed and plainclothes police officers for strict surveillance. (Dentsu dispatch, 1st)

Madrid: Today is International Labor Day. The authorities have taken special security measures to prevent incidents. The garrison troops were ordered to remain stationed in the camps, awaiting dispatch. Police posts in various places have also been strengthened. Local authorities in the provinces are also on high alert. Many suspicious people have been arrested in Asturias Province. Many trade unionists have been arrested in Barcelona. Last night at midnight, the city's tram lines were cut off. Someone plotted to assassinate General Batet, but the plot was revealed and failed. Four royalists were arrested on suspicion. The police in Barcelona are keeping silent about the matter. (Havas)

U.S. Silver Policy to Have a Surprising Move: Predictions from the U.S. Banking Sector 41

(New York) Wall Street researchers of silver trends now predict that the Treasury Department will make a surprising move when taking the next steps in its silver policy. Since the Treasury Department raised the price of silver, the monetary structure of Mexico has been shaken, and world speculation has followed. In view of this situation, the Treasury Department seems unwilling to act hastily. However, many say that the Treasury Department may be forced by pressure to reduce the value of silver dollars according to the gold standard ratio. This statement does not seem unfounded, because the world's supply of silver is not large, and the United States wants to implement Congress's silver policy, which it cannot do. If the price of silver is fixed at $2.18 per ounce, the problem would be easier to solve. If so, the Treasury Department's existing silver reserves, calculated at $1.29 per ounce, are worth about $145 million. If calculated at a price of $2.18 per ounce, it would be $245 million. In this case, the Treasury Department only needs to buy silver worth $41.5 million to establish a gold-silver ratio of three to one. Since the United States still needs to buy silver worth $41.5 million, it can use this to maintain the world price of silver and fulfill Congress's claims without allowing international speculators to manipulate and profit from it. The Treasury Department has not yet commented on its future plans, but Wall Street does not believe that it plans to gradually increase the price of silver and fill its treasury. This kind of procedure can never achieve the goal of a three-to-one gold-silver ratio, only prolongs the uncertain situation, and makes foreign speculators enjoy its benefits. For this reason, Wall Street predicts that the Treasury Department will change its policy. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

Portrait of Chinese Ambassador Guo Hanging in the Royal Academy Exhibition in London 42

(London) The Royal Academy exhibition will be open to the public tomorrow for private viewing. Among the exhibits is a portrait of Guo Taiqi, the Chinese Ambassador to the UK. The portrait was painted by a young artist named Green, who was introduced to Ambassador Guo by a professor from Oxford. The likeness is extremely accurate, and the exhibition committee considers it a fine work. This is the first time that a portrait of the Chinese Ambassador to the UK has been hung in Burlington House. (Reuters dispatch, 2nd)

Celebration of the British Monarch's Accession Will Proceed Rain or Shine 43

(London) According to today's news, the program for the celebration of the 25th anniversary of the accession of the British monarch on Monday, even if it rains on that day, will be implemented accordingly. However, if it rains, the British monarch and the royal family will go to St. Paul's Cathedral in sedan chairs instead of open carriages. The weather is very humid today, but the number of people gathering on the streets of London to view the decorations has not diminished slightly. The British monarch has today approved the military arrangements for the celebration day, which include selecting 14,000 soldiers from the Navy, Army, and Air Force to line up along the route that the British monarch will pass on that day. 12,000 police officers will be on duty in central London on Monday. The lighting of famous buildings and the 27 bonfires in London have all been completed today. The bonfire in Hyde Park will be lit by the British monarch himself at 9:55 p.m. It is estimated that there will be 1,750 bonfires across the country. Five addresses of congratulation to the British monarch, including one from Londonderry, will be carried to London tonight by Boy Scouts. The text will be relayed in turn. A total of 2,106 Boy Scouts will participate in this event, traveling 2,309 miles. It is estimated that there will be 4,000 representatives from all parts of the Empire invited to attend the thanksgiving service at St. Paul's Cathedral. (Reuters dispatch, 1st)

Overseas Chinese in London Establish the Chinese Children's Club: Fundraising Meeting Attracts Important Chinese and British Figures 44

(London) The Chinese Club, established here by overseas Chinese to benefit Chinese children, held a fundraising meeting today. Lady Astor specially lent the grand reception room of her St. James's Street residence as the venue. Those present included Privy Councillor Baldwin's wife and other distinguished guests. Then, Chinese Ambassador Guo Taiqi introduced entertainers, including Chinese short plays, music, and magic, which greatly interested the audience. After the entertainment, fundraising began, raising 140 pounds, half of which were annual donations. (Reuters dispatch, 30th)

(New York) The U.S. robot-piloted mystery plane completed its flight across the American continent today. The flight from Los Angeles on the Pacific coast directly to New York totaled 2,450 miles and lasted only 11 hours and 5 minutes, which is 20 minutes and 31 seconds less than the previous record. Although there were personnel on board during the flight, they did not provide guidance. (National News Agency dispatch, 30th)

Reuters Special Business Intelligence Telegram, May 2 46

Gold and Silver:

British Gold: The price of gold in London fell slightly due to the rise in the price of the pound. Today's price is 144 shillings and 4 pence, a decrease of 8 pence.

British Silver: The London silver market is currently uncertain due to the future actions of the U.S. Treasury Department, causing unease. Therefore, the price of silver plummeted today. The official list price for spot is 32 and 375 pence, down 2 and 125 pence; futures is 32 and a half pence, down 2 and 1875 pence. This is due to large-scale sales from China. It is reported that the United States and speculators bought in when the price fell. The silver market closed mixed.

American Silver: The price of silver in Monte Carlo fell 300 pounds today when the market opened.

Exchange Rates:

British-American: The London foreign exchange market had a lot of trading this morning. The British pound was firmer, and the opening exchange rate between the British pound and the U.S. dollar was $4.833125, which was 06.5 higher than the closing exchange rate between the U.S. dollar and the British pound yesterday. The price did not change much in the first hour, and then it became firmer. At noon, the British pound rose 125, and then rose another 3 pounds. At 2 p.m., it rose 375 to $4.84.

British-French: The opening price was 3 pounds lower, at 73 francs 22. In the first hour, it rose 5 pounds, at noon it rose 4 pounds, and at 2 p.m. it rose another 12 pounds to 73 francs 38.

Cotton and Wheat:

American Cotton: Trading in the New York cotton market was limited. Demand was low, so prices were weak. After the price of silver fell, there were long positions in the cotton market to close out.

British Cotton: The price in the Liverpool cotton market was slightly loose today. At 1 p.m., the July futures price was 6.48, down one pound.

British Wheat: The Liverpool wheat market fell today following the American wheat market. At 1 p.m., the July futures price was 5 shillings 6 pence 375, which was 875 lower than the previous close.

New York: The New York rubber market was not exciting and trended downward.

Securities:

New York: Before the New York securities market opened today, morale was very uncertain because there was no progress to stimulate new buying. However, the first quarter report of Chrysler Motors was excellent, so the company's stock price rose. The average price of the Dow Jones 20 Industrial Stocks opened 30 pounds higher, at 109.01. However, after the opening, prices fluctuated, and trading was still considerable. Silver mining stocks were quite weak because the Treasury Department's future actions had no firm indication, causing unease, and because the price of silver in London suddenly fell sharply. Central Standing Committee Decides on the Relocation and Burial of Martyr Liao Zhongkai; Sends Chen Zhaoying to Console the People in the Recovered Areas of Fujian; Nominates Wang Zhaoming to Report on the May 5th Memorial 47

(Nanjing) The Central Committee held its 169th Standing Committee meeting on the morning of the 2nd. The attendees included Ye Chucang, Wang Zhaoming, Ju Zheng, Lin Sen, Chu Minyi, Wang Maogong, Ding Chaowu, Zhang Zhen, Xiao Zhongzhen, Dai Kuisheng, Wu Tiecheng, Bai Wenwei, Deng Jiayan, Chen Gongbo, Zhang Huichang, Chen Zhaoying, Deng Feihuang, Chen Shuren, Gu Zhenggang, Duan Xipeng, Wang Luyi, Guo Chuntao, Xiao Jishan, Zeng Zhongming, Cheng Tianfang, Hong Ludong, Ma Chaojun, Chen Lifu, Miao Peicheng, Qin Zhen, Liang Hancao, Luo Jialun, Fu Rulin, Tang Youren, Ji Liang and others, more than thirty people. Ye Chucang presided over the meeting, and the following important cases were resolved: (1) Passed the Method for the Summer Party Ideology Education Discussion Conference for Primary School Teachers; (2) Sent Committee Member Chen Zhaoying to represent the Central Committee to console the people in the recovered bandit areas of Fujian; (3) Regarding the case of Mr. Liao Zhongkai's funeral, in addition to the state funeral ceremony, which was held on August 25th of the 14th year of the Republic, it should now be relocated and buried next to Dr. Sun Yat-sen's mausoleum in accordance with the decision of the Central Committee. The following methods are specifically decided: 1. Re-allocate 50,000 yuan for relocation and burial expenses; 2. Send a letter to the Mausoleum Management Committee to designate the relocation and burial site to facilitate planning; 3. Tentatively set the relocation and burial to be held in November of this year; 4. Ask the Mausoleum Management Committee to design the base construction, the main points of which are as follows: 1. The tomb should be in the Chinese style; 2. Build a monument and worship altar, etc.; 3. There is no need to build a sacrificial hall; (4) It is stipulated that all kinds of training classes organized by the provincial and municipal governments should have courses on party history and party ideology. The methods should be determined by the provincial and municipal party departments in consultation with the organizers; (5) Select a delegation of Boy Scouts from the country to participate in the 25th Anniversary National Jamboree of the Boy Scouts of America. The methods are to be determined by the Boy Scouts of China, and the budget should be submitted to the General Assembly for approval; (6) Ren Wenyiyou also concurrently serves as the custodian of the Overseas Chinese Donation Custody Committee; (7) Committee Member Wang Zhaoming will report on the May 5th Revolutionary Government Memorial; (8) Committee Member Ding Chaowu will report on the Central Memorial Week next Monday; (9) Others. (Central News Agency dispatch, 2nd)

Funing Huai River Diversion Project 50

Huaiyin: According to the latest investigation of the Huai River diversion project, the land in Funing is low-lying, and water seeps in very quickly. The project section is 23 kilometers long, which is one of the largest sections. Construction is the most difficult. Contrary to expectations, the number of workers applying for the current project has reached 33,000, exceeding the quota by as much as 8,000. Compared with the achievements of other counties, it is the best. However, although the drainage work is carried out day and night, the effectiveness is limited after all, which is a serious problem at present. (Special telegram, 2nd)

The Legislative Yuan Today Deliberated and Approved the International Postal Convention 54

(Nanjing) Our country's approval of the International Postal Convention and its accompanying agreements has been reviewed and finalized by the Foreign Affairs Committee of the Legislative Yuan and submitted to the plenary session of the Yuan on the morning of the 3rd for deliberation. According to the regulations of the International Postal Convention, revisions are made every five years. The one being deliberated by the Legislative Yuan this time is the amendment made at the 1934 International Postal Conference held in Cairo. Our country's representative to the conference has already signed the agreement, and the current procedure is for approval. This agreement has slight modifications compared to the 1929 London International Postal Convention. The main points are: reducing postal transit fees, abolishing mail landing fees, and stipulating that preparatory committee meetings will no longer be held before future International Postal Conferences. The Foreign Affairs Committee of the Legislative Yuan believes that the old London agreement has already been approved by the Yuan, and since the new Cairo agreement does not have many major changes compared to the old one, it can accommodate the opinions of both the Ministry of Foreign Affairs and the Ministry of Communications and should be approved. (3rd, Central News Agency dispatch)

The Ministry of Industry Plans to Formulate a Patent Law 55

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry plans to establish a Patent Bureau and, according to the schedule, should formulate a Patent Law this year. However, due to the difference between our country's industrial situation and those of other countries in the world, this law, which has a global nature, must be studied for a long time before a draft can be prepared. Currently, the Ministry is first instructing provinces and cities to organize invention research institutes, which has led to the mistaken rumor that a Patent Bureau is being established. (2nd, special dispatch)

Measures for Recasting Silver Ingots from the Public 56

(Nanjing) According to the Ministry of Finance, the Central Bank's handling of silver ingot exchange affairs has ended upon the expiration of the term. After the closure of the exchange program, if the public possesses silver ingots, they can request the Central Mint to recast them into silver coins. (2nd, Central News Agency dispatch)

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance believes that the abolition of taels and the adoption of the yuan has been in effect for two years. Those who possess silver ingots can exchange them for silver coins at the Central Bank within a limited time. Now that the deadline has passed, the Central Bank has announced the closure of the exchange program. Hereafter, anyone with silver ingots can request the Central Mint to recast them into silver coins. (2nd, special dispatch)

The Examination Yuan Held a Regular Meeting Yesterday 57

(Nanjing) The Examination Yuan held its 163rd meeting on the 2nd to discuss and decide on the Ministry of Industry's proposed revision of the Regulations for the Registration of Agricultural, Industrial, and Mining Technicians and Assistant Technicians. Before the promulgation of regulations for various specialized professions or technical personnel examinations, the first article of the regulations should include a category for those who have passed the general examination for construction personnel. After the promulgation of the regulations for specialized professions, etc., examinations should be conducted in accordance with those regulations. The Yuan continued to discuss and amend important cases such as various types of examination regulations. (2nd, Central News Agency dispatch)

The Executive Yuan Reviews the Draft Publication Law 58

(Nanjing) The Executive Yuan convened a review meeting at 3 PM on the afternoon of the 2nd. Representatives from the Ministries of Interior, Foreign Affairs, and Education attended. It is reported that the meeting reviewed the internally revised draft Publication Law. After two hours of discussion, the draft will be submitted to the Central Political Council after being approved by the Executive Yuan, which will then pass it on to the Legislative Yuan for deliberation, and then it will be promulgated and implemented. The old Publication Law will be repealed. This is expected to occur in a few months. (2nd, Central News Agency dispatch)

Ministry of Communications Does Not Plan to Change Measures for Sampan Inspection 62

(Nanjing) The second sampan inspection is being carried out in various places. The Tianjin Maritime Affairs Bureau also proposed implementing an inspection system in three seasons: spring, summer, and autumn. The Ministry of Communications has already reported to the Executive Yuan and the Control Yuan that the various fees for sampan inspection and registration are evenly distributed over three years for recordkeeping. The requests from various bureaus are not easy to change rashly, and the order is to comply with the original regulations. (2nd, special dispatch)

Performance Appraisal Law to be Implemented on Schedule 63

(Nanjing) The Performance Appraisal Law drafted by the Ministry of Personnel is currently being reviewed by the Legislative Yuan. The Ministry plans to implement it starting in July, stipulating that central, provincial, and municipal agencies will conduct a small performance appraisal once a year and a large performance appraisal every three years. Those with excellent performance will be promoted and receive salary increases and awards, while those with poor performance will be dismissed, demoted, have their salaries deducted, and receive warnings. (2nd, special dispatch)

Headquarters Formulates Measures for Providing Relief to Residents in Recovered Areas 88

(Hankou) The headquarters has formulated 14 measures for providing food relief to residents in counties recovered from banditry, telegraphed to the eight provinces of Hubei, Hunan, Jiangxi, Yunnan, Guizhou, Sichuan, Shaanxi, and Gansu for compliance. The telegram states that the northern and southern borders of Sichuan have long been plagued by bandits, and there is concern about food shortages at this time of year when the new harvest has not yet arrived. The border areas of Yunnan, Guizhou, Hubei, Shaanxi, and Gansu, which are adjacent to each other, are also mostly areas disturbed by bandits, and food shortages are likely inevitable. After each bandit-affected county is recovered, the most important task is to address the food problem. If regulations are not clearly defined and remedies are not properly planned, there will be no way to deal with the aftermath once food is scarce. Therefore, the measures for providing food relief to residents in counties recovered from banditry are formulated, hoping that you will comply accordingly. (2nd, special dispatch)

Song told the Central News Agency reporter that his visit, in addition to signing the hydropower loan contract, was also to visit the newly recovered areas. As for the electricity aspect, in addition to improving the existing equipment, a new power plant will be added. (1st, Central News Agency dispatch)

The Remnants of Zhu and Mao's Bandits Fled to the Yunnan Border and Were Surrounded; The Northern Sichuan Campaign Proceeds Smoothly; General Hu's Forces Capture Pingwu; Zhang Xueliang Reports to Chiang Kai-shek on His Trip to Henan 108

Hankou Correspondence: Zhu and Mao's bandit remnants were fiercely attacked in Guizhou, suffering heavy losses. They then fled south along Baiyan, attempting to invade the Zhubian area. However, the National Army relentlessly pursued and attacked, giving them no respite. They changed their plans again, fleeing west through Qipan Mountain to Guangshun, Ziyun, Zhenfeng, and Xingren counties, which were subsequently recovered by the National Army. The bandits had no foothold in Guizhou Province. One group fled from Xingyi and another from Panxian to the Qujing, Zhan'yi, and Xundian areas of Yunnan Province. The losses along the way were countless. Since the bandits left Guizhou Province, the remaining bandits were quickly suppressed, and local reconstruction was carried out. Li Yunjie's troops arrived in Guiyang, awaiting orders to pursue the bandits. Wang Jialie's and Wu Qiwai's troops advanced west across Ziyun and Xingren, encircling the bandits on three sides. The fighting has been fierce in recent days, with many bandits killed. The bandits' fleeing to Yunnan is both to escape the National Army's pursuit and to attempt to cross the Jinsha River and sneak into western Sichuan, gradually plotting to join forces with Xu Xiangqian's bandits. This plan had previously been attempted and failed, and now they are repeating the same mistake, which shows that they are at the end of their rope. On the northern Sichuan front, fierce battles have also been taking place in recent days. Xu Xiangqian's bandits fiercely attacked Zitong, Zhongba, Jiangyou, and Weicheng in dozens of large and small battles, but were all repelled by Deng Xihou's troops. They then concentrated their forces to attack Jiangyou alone, and built fortifications near Guandu and Jiangcheng, indicating a long siege. Yang Shaixuan's brigade of Deng's troops is also making every effort to resist. The people are supplying the troops with food and supplies, and are united in defense. The bandits cannot succeed. Yang Shuxian's brigade is stationed in Qinggangpu, and Gong's brigade is stationed in Maodong, forming a strategic position with Jiangyou. Chen Dingxun's reinforcements arrived in Mianyang via Yanting and immediately joined the front line. As a result, the morale of the Jiangyou defenders is greatly boosted. Although the bandits are brave and fierce, they cannot cross the Fujiang River. North of Jiangyou, Hu Zongnan's division captured the Motianling position on the 28th of last month and advanced to the Tangjiahe-Qingchuan line, capturing Pingwu County in one day. One part of this division, together with the troops of Commander Diao of Deng's army, captured Wulong Mountain. The National Army also occupies an absolute advantage in the upper reaches of the Fujiang River, and Cangxi on the east bank of the Jialing River has also been recovered by the National Army. The bandits are indeed surrounded on all sides, and it is expected that they can be wiped out between Jiangyou and Zitong in a few days and will no longer be a major threat.

Furthermore, Zhang Xueliang, the Director of the Provisional Headquarters sent by Chiang Kai-shek to inspect the Henan and Shaanxi armies, returned to Hubei from Guiyang on the 17th of last month, flew to Kaifeng on the 23rd, went from Kaifeng to Xi'an on the 24th, and returned to Hankou on the 27th. In addition to the inspection, he also met with Liu Zhi and Yang Hucheng to discuss the suppression of the remaining bandits in the border areas and the bandit suppression issues in Sichuan and Shaanxi. In Hubei, he also handled important official matters of the provisional headquarters. Only on the 1st of this month did he take a Ford aircraft to Guiyang to report to Chiang Kai-shek on the progress of his trip. After staying for a few days, he returned to Hubei to take charge. (May 1st)

He Yingqin Arrives in Jinan; Tours Scenic Spots; Inspects Garrison Troops 109

Jinan Correspondence: He Yingqin, the Minister of Military Administration and Acting Chairman of the Peiping Military Council, arrived in Jinan by special train from Peiping on the afternoon of the 28th to inspect the situation in Shandong Province. Having received prior notice, Han Fuqu specially sent Liu Shuxiang, the Chief of Staff of the Third Route Army Headquarters, to Dezhou on the evening of the 28th to greet him on the special train. On the morning of the 29th, the whole city was decorated with flags. At around 7:00 am, Han Fuqu led representatives from all sectors of the Party, government, and military to welcome him at the station. Security was tight inside and outside the station. Temporary additions to the welcoming party included Men Zhizhong, a member of the Military Council; Ge Guangting, Chairman of the Jiaoji Railway; Tang Xiang, Director of the Shandong-Henan Joint Tax Bureau; and representatives from Qingdao Mayor Shen Honglie and the Third Fleet Commander Xie Gangzhe. The welcoming lines on the platform were extremely orderly, with the army in the East Station, followed by the provincial government agencies, then the Party headquarters, and the West Station being for the public organizations. At 8:30 am, He's special train entered the station. The troops presented arms, and other personnel removed their hats to salute. He, wearing a military uniform, got off the train, shook hands with the welcomers, and went to the Jinpu Railway Hotel temporary headquarters to rest. The important figures of the provincial government hosted a banquet for He in the East Building of the provincial government in the evening, and performed plays to add to the enjoyment. On the morning of the 30th, He inspected the garrison troops and gave a speech in Xinzhuang. The Provincial Party Headquarters, the Municipal Government, and various public organizations originally planned to host a banquet at Thousand Buddha Mountain on the afternoon of the 30th, but later temporarily changed it to Jinde Society. In the afternoon, He also inspected the ordnance factory. It was decided that he would take a special train to Qingdao at 9:00 pm on the 30th. After arriving in Jinan, He made the following statement: "I have been in Beiping for more than two years and have long wanted to come to Shandong to see the construction situation in Shandong Province, but due to busy affairs, I have not been able to fulfill my wish. Recently, the affairs have been slightly simplified, so I took the time to come to Shandong for inspection, and also to see the troops stationed in Jinan. If time permits, I will also go to Qingdao to inspect the municipal situation. Chairman Han's achievements in governing Shandong are well known far and wide. Mayor Shen has also done a lot of construction for Qingdao. I believe that I will definitely get a very good impression during this trip to Shandong. Chairman Chiang has successively promoted the New Life Movement and the National Economic Construction Movement, both of which are necessary plans for a modern country. Chairman Han has vigorously promoted these two movements. I hope that the officials and people of Shandong Province will work hard to implement these two movements under the leadership of Chairman Han." (30th)

Severe Drought in Shandong Province; Wheat Half Wilts Away — Fortunately, Wheat Prices Are Stable and People's Hearts Are at Peace — 110

Jinan Correspondence: This spring, the province is suffering from a severe drought. Water is like gold, and the wheat in the fields is rarely able to avoid wilting. It is already past the season when river water or well water can be used for irrigation. Counties where well digging is not widespread can only watch their crops wither and die. Farmers are worried and sighing. The wheat is now less than a foot tall, and the ears of wheat are particularly small and insignificant. Even if it rains now, the harvest will be no more than 50%. The disaster is already apparent throughout the province. According to past practice, wheat prices should soar, and people's food supply should be in panic. However, this year is an exception. The reasons are: (1) Tight financial conditions mean that grain stores do not buy and store much. (2) Flour sales are sluggish in the market, with each bag only costing two yuan and seventy-odd cents, so flour mills are also unwilling to buy more. (3) Those who store wheat are in urgent need of money and are rushing to sell it. Due to these reasons, wheat prices are still stable. Statistics show that there are 9,280 tons of wheat stored in Jinan. In another forty days, the new wheat will be on the market, which will be sufficient to supply the market, so there is no need to worry about shortages. People's hearts are still at peace. (1st)

Songjiang: Several Robberies Occur Outside the South Gate in One Night 111

Datieqiao Township, outside the South Gate of this city, is four or five li from the city. The previous night (30th) at midday, the family of Yu Asan, a villager in the Seventeenth Tu Township of Xijing, was robbed. He had agreed to sell his land for 320 yuan and was drawing up a contract at home. The broker, Feng Xinglou, was also present. Suddenly, more than a dozen robbers, carrying handguns, iron rulers, wooden sticks, and other weapons, broke in. They forbade anyone from making a sound and forced them to change the contract price. However, according to Songjiang customs, the full price is not paid when drawing up a contract. The robbers' demands were not met, and Feng Xinglou was shot and wounded when he tried to raise the alarm. He was sent to Rongcheng Hospital, where Zhang Shaoxiu used surgical techniques to treat him, and his life is not in danger. Yu Asan's wife, Yu Zhangshi, was burned by the robbers, and his uncle, Yu Youtang, was also beaten and injured. As a result, they were all sent to Rongcheng Hospital for treatment. On the same night, the family of Fa Gu Xiangbao in the same area was also robbed. When Gu saw the robbers coming, he threw a stool at them. The robbers fired a gun, and the bullet hit his scrotum, causing him to die. At around 12:00 am on the same night, seven or eight robbers, armed with wooden shoulder poles and wooden sticks, their heads covered with towels, broke into the home of Gu Xiansheng in the Fourteenth Tu outside the South Gate. They ransacked the house. Gu Xiansheng shouted for the police, and the robbers used weapons to injure his left hand, fracturing the bones and causing him great pain. The township head, Gao Zhongkui, has reported the incident to the district office, stating that robberies are frequent so close to the city, causing the people to lose sleep. He requested that the matter be forwarded to the county government for investigation. It is also reported that the injured Gu Xiangbao has died from his injuries.

Jiading: Bank Theft Occurs Again 112

After a major theft occurred at the Jiading Commercial Savings Bank on South Main Street in the city on March 9th, a reward of 1,000 yuan was offered for information leading to the arrest of the thieves, but the case has not yet been solved. Yesterday (1st) night, another theft occurred at the Jiading Farmers Bank on East Main Street. The bank building is rented from the Education Bureau and a sturdy wall was specially built when the bank was established. That night, a small thief climbed over the wall from the Yi Nong lane behind the bank into the compound of the Baptist Church, then dug through two walls on the east side of the bank belonging to the Dai family. From the Dai family's courtyard, he dug west through the wall next to the bank's east side and entered. In the manager's office, he pried open the iron safe and then pried open three small drawers inside. He used special tools, so the key parts of the lock were destroyed, while the other non-essential parts remained intact. This shows that it was done by a very professional thief. However, the bank's savings were stored in a separate, sturdy vault. The safe that the thief opened only contained important documents, which had been returned to the vault the evening before. However, the Nanshu Tian Fu Collection Office had sent over 76 yuan in collected land tax to be deposited in the county treasury, which was stored in that safe and was stolen. After the theft, the thief exited through the same hole in the wall. This morning at 5:00 am, a bank employee discovered the theft and immediately reported it to the County Public Security Bureau for investigation.

Wuxi: Large Quantity of Silkworm Eggs Arrive 113

This year, the county is short of spring silkworm eggs. The Canrong Model District has ordered Japanese silkworm eggs to meet the market demand. Now, 10,000 sheets of Japanese silkworm eggs have been shipped to Wuxi. It is scheduled to begin selling them today (3rd). Each villager is limited to buying one sheet. However, the weather has been erratic recently. A few days ago, it was extremely hot, and the early spring silkworms in the villages had already hatched. In recent days, the early spring silkworms have even begun to enter the first sleep stage, and the sudden cold weather has affected their development. Fortunately, the weather is clear and sunny, so there is no major problem. As for the late spring silkworms, they have not yet hatched. It is said that some unscrupulous merchants in the Dongting Town area of the Second District are taking advantage of the shortage of spring silkworm eggs and the villagers' urgent need to manufacture inferior silkworm eggs privately, which have not been inspected by the Model District, and are selling them at high prices to make a profit.

In the Fanghua Temple area of the Eighth Bao, Ninety-eighth Tu in Zhou Tanqiao, Third District of the county, a village woman named Zhu Huangshi had an argument with her neighbor Xu Zixuan over a grave site during the Qingming Festival this year. The next morning, her son, Zhu Hongsheng, searched everywhere, but could not find her. However, at noon the day before yesterday, the body of Zhu Huangshi was suddenly found in a deep pool in the river in front of Xu's house. Her head was resting on the beach, which was a strange sight. The villagers all believe that Xu Zixuan is a major suspect. City News

Literacy Campaign Promotion Week - Opening Ceremony Held This Morning 118

Education Bureau Director Pan Reports, Chairman Wu Issues Instructions. Yesterday Was Radio Broadcast Promotion Day, Today Is Business Community Promotion.

The Shanghai Municipality held the opening ceremony for the Literacy Education Promotion Week, as well as the inauguration ceremony for the directors of the various district offices and the heads of the service group branches. This morning at nine o'clock, the event was held at the auditorium of the Municipal Central District Zhengzhong Elementary School. Chairman Wu Tiecheng, Education Bureau Director Pan Gongzhan, the directors of various districts, the heads of various group branches, and all staff of the Literacy Education Association attended. Details are recorded as follows:

Attendees Those present included Chairman Wu Tiecheng, Deputy Chairman Pan Gongzhan, Committee Members Wu Kaixian, Zeng Shengdian, Chen Gongsu, Jiang Jianbai, Ma Chonggan, Xie Engao, Feng Kui, Li Suixian, Tong Xingbai, General Secretary Tao Baichuan, Directors of District Offices Lu Hairun, Tao Guangchuan, Jiang Wenbao, Chen Banchun, Heads of Service Group Branches Yan Zhenyu, Sheng Zhensheng, Cheng Kuanzheng, Gu Yinqian, Xu Shushen, Guests Zhang Chengzhi of the Songhu Garrison Headquarters, Liu Zhaoxing of the Wusong Municipal Office, Chen Ce of the Security Committee, Zhou Zhicheng of the Municipal Public Security Bureau, Hu Changzhi of the Health Bureau, Shui Xiangyun of the Municipal Federation of Trade Unions, Zhao Shusheng of the Chinese Labor Association, Wu Chuijiu of the Jiangwan Municipal Committee Office, Chen Jixi of the Land Bureau, Feng Chengqiu of the Public Utilities Bureau, and over four hundred others.

Chairman's Address After the ceremonial proceedings, Chairman Pan Gongzhan delivered the opening remarks, stating, "Today is the first day of the Literacy Promotion Week designated by the Municipal Literacy Committee. The directors of the district offices and the heads of the service group branches will also be jointly sworn in today. Everyone understands the importance and significance of literacy education. It is hoped that the directors and group leaders will be responsible for activities within their respective districts under the command of the General Office, and recognize this work as the most important. From today onward, we must proceed diligently according to the prescribed methods. All municipal and registered private schools should lead their students to help those who are illiterate become literate, and vigorously implement literacy education to achieve completion as scheduled."

Wu's Instructions After the Chairman's report, the swearing-in ceremony was held. Chairman Wu delivered instructions, saying, "Fellow gentlemen and comrades, today is May 1st, Labor Day. The Shanghai Municipal Literacy Education Committee has specifically designated today as the first day of Literacy Education Promotion Week, which is of great significance. Ninety percent of the people in our country are poor laborers. If we want to build the country, we must have the concerted efforts of all the people to succeed. But if we want the concerted efforts of all the people to build our country, we must first educate all the people to recognize characters, have knowledge, know that they have a country and a nation, and be able to work hard for the country and the nation. Among the 450 million people in our country, those engaged in direct production, such as workers and farmers, account for the vast majority. This vast majority of direct producers is the main force in maintaining the survival of our entire nation. But this vast majority of people are illiterate and lack knowledge. How can we enable them to increase production and improve production? Of course, it is impossible. Therefore, it has formed the alarming phenomenon in our country today. Premier Sun, in his Principles of Livelihood, told us that China's import surplus today has reached as much as 400 or 500 million yuan, and in less than ten years, it will reach 1 billion yuan. Now, in less than ten years, the import surplus has reached 700 million yuan. Our current way of life is different from the past, but our production methods are still the same as in the Middle Ages, and the output is even less than before. How do we know this? Because we see from the customs reports that the largest import from foreign countries every year is agricultural products. We Chinese people do not understand modern production methods, but even the greatest skill passed down by our ancestors, the method of farming, is almost lost now. Take Guangdong as an example, Guangdong Province has to take 1 million silver dollars to Siam and Annam to buy rice every year. At the same time, Hunan Province had a lot of rice left over that year, and although the price was cheap, it was not transported due to inconvenient transportation, and it could only be left to rot. Isn't this a very contradictory and strange phenomenon? The origin of this contradictory and dangerous phenomenon is due to the fact that the vast majority of direct producers, the workers and farmers in our country, have no knowledge and are illiterate. Therefore, our urgent task at present is to teach this majority of direct producers to read and improve their knowledge. Therefore, the Shanghai Municipal Government announced that it would implement literacy education on July 10th of this year, and designated today, May 1st, as the opening day of the Literacy Education Promotion Week and the inauguration ceremony for the directors of the district offices and the heads of the literacy education service groups. The significance of this is evident. Among the 450 million compatriots in China, 80% are illiterate. Even in the Shanghai urban area, which has the advantage of being at the forefront of the country and is the cultural and economic center of the country, 30% are illiterate. This is the greatest shame of our nation, the greatest stain on our nation, and the root cause of national humiliation and the most serious national crisis in history. In other words, national humiliation and national crisis are caused and formed by the shame of having 80% of the people illiterate. People across the country, especially patriotic people, are running around and shouting slogans every day to wash away national humiliation and save the country from crisis. But the fundamental plan to wash away national humiliation and save the country is to solve the problem of illiteracy of 80% of the people in the country first, and in Shanghai, to solve the problem of illiteracy of 30% of the people in the city first. If the people of the whole country can make concerted efforts to solve the problem of illiteracy of 80% of the people in the country, then they can wash away national humiliation and save the country. At the same time, we must also be able to make concerted efforts to solve the problem of illiteracy of 30% of the people in Shanghai, so that we can look forward to the prosperity and development of Shanghai. None of us are born literate, and none of us are born with knowledge. But why do some people have the opportunity to receive education, and some people do not have the opportunity to receive education? Why do some people have knowledge, and some people do not have knowledge? Why do some people have food to eat, and some people do not have food to eat? Why do some people sit and have food to eat, and some people have to work all day to have food to eat? This is entirely due to the different circumstances of their families, social environments, and personal experiences, which have led to these differences. We have the opportunity to receive education and have food to eat. Most of these superior opportunities are given to us by society. For example, when comparing Shanghai with the inland areas, the inland areas have more than 80% illiterate people, while Shanghai only has 30%. This is not because the people in the inland areas are less talented than those in Shanghai, but because the people in Shanghai have better opportunities to receive education than those in the inland areas. But we must know that it is meaningless for a small number of people to receive education and become literate. If a small number of people can live a stable life, but the majority of people cannot live a stable life, then the lives of the small number of people will not be stable in the end. Therefore, since a small number of us have these opportunities, we should be aware of them, not fail to live up to them, and cherish them. That is, the small number of literate people must be responsible for teaching the majority of illiterate people, and must make direct and indirect efforts to find ways to stabilize and improve the lives of the majority of people. Shanghai has a relatively concentrated talent pool, relatively abundant financial resources, and relatively complete facilities, and has a variety of superior positions and environments. This time, when we promote literacy education, we must make it a success and never let it fail. Because the success or failure of Shanghai's literacy education is directly related to the success or failure of the national literacy education movement. Shanghai has such a superior position and environment. If the literacy movement cannot succeed and ends in failure, then the literacy education movement in other parts of the country will not only fail to succeed, but also will not be able to be promoted. Therefore, this time, Shanghai's literacy education must be successful. The success or failure of this is related to our entire country and nation. At the same time, whether Shanghai's promotion is effective this time can also test whether our Shanghai intellectual class, especially those in the education sector, can fulfill their natural duty to teach illiterate people, and can also test whether the Shanghai Kuomintang comrades can work hard on the basic task of national rejuvenation, the literacy education movement, and can also test whether the city's civil servants are earnestly promoting it. Therefore, this literacy education movement requires the mobilization of all, whether it is the intellectual class, the education sector, the Kuomintang comrades, or the civil servants, to earnestly take on this responsibility, work hard to promote it, and must promote it effectively. I sincerely follow the intellectual class, the education sector, all the comrades in the city, and all the civil servants in the city to fulfill my personal obligations and fulfill my personal natural duty. I hope that the citizens of the city will unanimously and earnestly promote the literacy movement in order to achieve the complete success of this movement."

Tong's Speech Then, the representative of the Municipal Party Headquarters, Tong Xingbai, delivered a speech, saying, "Everyone, today you are holding the inauguration ceremony. I have a few opinions and contributions. (1) Today, you are all people in the education sector, great people in the education sector, who can give people sufficient knowledge and skills and enable them to survive in the world. However, literacy education is different from ordinary education, because the target of education is different. The difficulty and promotion of literacy education should be known to all. We must break through the difficulties and enable them to read. Its greatness should be even greater than trying our best in ordinary education. Today, in addition to bearing the responsibility of striving for ordinary education, you also bear the mission of promoting literacy education, so you will definitely be able to exert its full greatness in the future. This is what the education sector itself should strive for. (2) Today's society must not be selfish and self-interested. If the country and the nation have one more member and get nothing, then I am no different from weeds and rotten things. We must seek the happiness of the whole society in addition to seeking our own survival. This is the meaning of life, and in the cause of seeking the happiness of the whole society, promoting literacy education is the most urgent task. Because making the illiterate literate and giving the opportunity to those who do not have the opportunity to become literate is the meaning of life that everyone should strive for. Literacy education is one of the seven movements of our party, and it is also the central work of the Water Party. This time, the municipal government has mobilized many talents with great determination. The Municipal Party Headquarters will also do its best for this movement. In addition to assisting the municipal government, the district party headquarters and district branches will establish literacy schools, and various social organizations will also establish schools. There are three types of people in society today. The first type of people do not understand the meaning of literacy education and the methods we are promoting. The second type of people are skeptical or opposed to literacy education. The third type of people already understand literacy education, but are unwilling to actively participate. Therefore, we must publicize to make the first type of people understand, the second type of people agree, and the third type of people participate. This is the purpose of this association's publicity. The content of the literacy education we are running includes three types: literacy education, common sense guidance, and civic training. The promotion methods are divided into two types. The first type is to set up 220 literacy schools, each school runs six classes, a total of 1,320 classes, each class enrolls 50 people, graduates in two months, reads one hour a day, and it is estimated that 400,000 illiterate people can become literate in a year. The textbook has been compiled, and the content is simple and interesting. The second type is to organize a literacy education service group. All middle school students and older elementary school students participate, and there will be a total of 10,000 members. After giving them appropriate training, they will go to various places to guide and teach people to read. Each person teaches at least two illiterate people in two months, and can also teach more than 100,000 people in a year. In this way, with both sides proceeding, all illiterate people in Shanghai can be eliminated in one year."

Guangdong Delegation Arrives in Shanghai by Ship Yesterday Afternoon 121

Staying in Shanghai for Three Days Before Going to Hangzhou, Returning to Shanghai to Proceed to Beijing and Various Other Locations

The Guangdong Provincial Government, in order to understand the conditions of civil administration, economy, construction, and education in various provinces and cities across the country, has specially organized a Guangdong Provincial Government Inspection Delegation to visit various provinces and cities for the purpose of learning and drawing lessons. The delegation, led by Li Yupei and comprising eleven members, arrived in Shanghai yesterday afternoon at 1:00 PM aboard the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's "Haili" ship, docking at Jinliyuan Wharf. Chen Jitang's representative in Beijing, Yang Dezhao, and others welcomed them at the port. After disembarking, the delegation members checked into the New Asia Hotel and plan to stay in Shanghai for three days, visiting the construction of the Greater Shanghai Plan before proceeding to cities such as Beijing and Hangzhou for inspection. The details are recorded as follows:

Delegation Members Arriving in Shanghai The delegation consists of thirteen members in total. Those who arrived in Shanghai yesterday include Li Yupei, Li Getian, Zhong Shenglin, Zhang Gangqun, Deng Runkang, Song Dejian, Zeng Guoguang, He Zhongchun, Du Zhanjin, Chen Zonghai, and Wen Kewei, totaling eleven individuals. Li Huaishuang and Ma Pei are still in Guangdong preparing everything. Li and Ma will be traveling to Tibet for inspection, so they are scheduled to go to Hong Kong within days and take a ship to India before entering Tibet for inspection.

Inspection Itinerary After arriving in Shanghai yesterday, the delegation plans to stay in Shanghai for three days to inspect everything. They are also scheduled to visit the central urban area this morning to see the construction plan of Greater Shanghai. After completing the inspection in Shanghai, they will proceed to Hangzhou, and then from Hangzhou, they will go to various counties in Zhejiang Province to inspect the construction of highways and other infrastructure in the province. After completing the inspection in Zhejiang Province, they will take the route through Shanghai to Beijing, and then travel north along the Tianjin-Pukou Railway to Jinan, Qingdao, Tianjin, and Beiping for inspection. After that, they will travel west from Beiping to Taiyuan, Xi'an, and Luoyang, and then south to Hankou, Changsha, and Hunan Province for inspection. After completing the inspection in Hunan, they will travel east along the Yangtze River to Jiujiang and Nanchang, and are scheduled to return to the province from Jiangxi. The inspection period is two months.

Current Situation in Guangdong Province Yesterday, a reporter from the Central News Agency visited the delegation at the New Asia Hotel and inquired about the inspection mission. Delegation member Li Yupei responded as follows: Since the implementation of the three-year plan in Guangdong Province, two and a half years have passed. In order to understand the actual situation of civil administration and construction in various provinces and cities across the country, and to learn from it, the Guangdong Provincial Government Inspection Delegation was organized. The scope of the inspection includes four aspects: finance, civil administration, construction, and education in various provinces and cities. As for rumors that the inspection involves military affairs, those are not confirmed information. The inspection period and itinerary have already been determined as mentioned earlier. Li continued to describe the current status of the three-year construction plan in Guangdong Province, saying that the three-year construction plan in Guangdong Province is now 80% complete. The three-year plan originally planned to establish 24 factories within the three-year period, and 20 have now been established, including three sugar factories, two in Guangzhou and one in Huizhou, and it is also planned to establish two factories each in Chaozhou and Shantou, one fertilizer factory, two cement factories, one ammonium acetate factory, one alcohol factory, one soda factory, and one textile factory. The textile factory is further divided into four factories, including cotton and silk (already established), linen and wool (to be established). Other projects such as steel factories, hydropower plants, etc., are all in the planning stage. In terms of Guangdong's finances, the annual revenue is 100 million, while the expenditure reaches 110 million, with a shortfall of 10 million. This is all due to the establishment of a large number of factories, which is expected to be offset in the future. Guangdong's tax revenue also follows the central government's strict implementation of abolishing excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, and has now abolished more than 200 types of excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies. As for education funds, they were more than 2 million three years ago, and have now more than doubled. Therefore, production schools and vocational schools in the province are no longer as rare as they used to be. Regarding Guangdong's finances, the authorities, due to insufficient financial revenue and expenditure, and the abolition of excessive taxes and miscellaneous levies, plan to levy a temporary land tax. In terms of construction, more than 37,000 kilometers of highways have been built, and long-distance telephones have reached more than 40,000 li. Other construction projects are also in active progress.

Overseas Chinese Federation Publishes the Truth about the Anti-Chinese Situation in Siam 124

Three Million Overseas Chinese Compatriots Will Become Aliens; It Is Hoped That the Government Will Negotiate and Conclude a Commercial Treaty Quickly

The Overseas Chinese Federation yesterday published the truth about the anti-Chinese situation in Siam and its response methods. The text states: China and Siam have deep relations in terms of culture, economy, and even blood relations. There are now more than 3 million Overseas Chinese in Siam, accounting for more than a quarter of the total population of Siam, and accounting for one-third of the total number of Overseas Chinese in the world. However, China and Siam have not yet established formal diplomatic relations, so the Siamese government only has unilateral actions in dealing with Overseas Chinese, with no bilateral consultations at all. Therefore, matters of excluding Overseas Chinese are often heard. When the new Siamese government was established, it recognized the great power of the Overseas Chinese and decided to implement various anti-Chinese policies and promulgate them as laws and regulations. If these policies are indeed implemented, Overseas Chinese will have no place to stand in Siam within a few years. The most important anti-Chinese policies of the Siamese government are listed below:

Promulgation of the New Immigration Law Siam's first immigration law was promulgated in 1927, stipulating that Overseas Chinese residents pay an entry tax of five Siamese cents, plus a handling fee of six cents and five thousandths, and restricting those suffering from eye diseases from entering the country. The immigration law was revised in 1931, increasing the entry tax to ten cents, plus a handling fee of twelve cents and fifty tenths, and also levying a residence tax of thirty cents. Overseas Chinese leaving Siam had to pay back the Siamese passport fee of five cents, and were limited to returning to Siam within two years, otherwise they would be treated as new immigrants. The second revision of the immigration law in 1933 increased the residence fee to one hundred cents, and the return to Siam passport fee was also increased to twenty cents, and the time limit was changed to one year, and those who were illiterate were restricted from entering the country. Recently, there have been even more intensified news.

Destruction of Overseas Chinese Industry and Commerce In recent years, the commercial regulations promulgated have restricted the operation of Overseas Chinese exchange businesses, pawnshops, second-hand goods businesses, and rickshaw businesses, or levied heavy taxes. Recently, the People's Party has been in power, and the crackdown has been even more severe. The Ministry of Internal Affairs has now been established, and has drafted a new economic plan. Although it has not been fully implemented, in May of last year, the Siamese government planned to establish a large state-run fire brigade and planned to nationalize the fire brigades and rice mills in the country. (According to statistics, Overseas Chinese account for 90% of the operation of Siamese rice mills.) In addition, the newly promulgated fisheries regulations restrict non-Siamese from operating, causing tens of thousands of Overseas Chinese industrial and commercial people engaged in fishing to lose their jobs. (3) Implementation of

Assimilation Policy In 1918, the Siamese government promulgated the Private School Regulations, stipulating that Overseas Chinese-run schools, in addition to registering with the Siamese Ministry of Education, the principal must have a Siamese high school sophomore qualification. There are very few qualified Overseas Chinese, so the principals of each school are all Siamese. Teachers must pass the examination before they can be employed. In 1932, the Compulsory Education Regulations were promulgated, stipulating that children aged seven to fourteen (including Overseas Chinese children) should all enter compulsory schools. All Chinese schools must, as usual, teach Siamese language for 25 hours per week. In 1933, it was further stipulated that students who should receive compulsory education should all be transferred to Siamese schools and should no longer enter Chinese schools. The crackdown on Chinese school teachers has become more and more severe. In addition to stipulating that they must first pass the Siamese language and examination, they must also fill out their resumes, submit certificates and diplomas, and submit fingerprints of all ten fingers. In fact, it has not been applied to schools run by British, French, American, and Japanese personnel. Last year, they even used the excuse that the Siamese language of the school teachers was unqualified and the management was not good.

Closing More Than Sixty Chinese Schools The above three points can be seen that the anti-Chinese policy of the Siamese government is truly all-encompassing and step-by-step. The implementation of the first point of the New Immigration Law means that Chinese entering the country need 200 Chinese currency per person, including boat fare, and must be literate. Because most of the Chinese who go to Siam are laborers, most of them are illiterate and cannot afford this heavy fee. I ask how many people can still go to the South Seas? Therefore, since the promulgation of the immigration law, the number of Chinese entering the country has greatly decreased, which is the actual proof. As for the second item, after the implementation of the so-called new economic policy, the most affected is the fire battle industry. 90% of the rice mill industry in Siam is operated by Chinese, which can also be said to be the largest economic right of Chinese merchants. If the rice mill is nationalized, it is tantamount to completely eliminating the economic status of Overseas Chinese. The assimilation policy in the first item is even more vicious, and the price examples of education for foreign nationals in various countries are also extremely

Absurd and Unparalleled Internationally, there has never been a case where foreign education is not allowed to set up schools and teach their own languages ​​and characters. The Siamese government's move directly closes Chinese schools completely and makes hundreds of thousands of Chinese children learn to be Siamese and forget the culture of their motherland. Its cruelty is truly unparalleled. The Siamese government's exclusion of Overseas Chinese is clearly demonstrated. This time, the Siamese Far East Tourism Corps denied that there was any anti-Chinese matter and dared not explicitly state the truth of its implementation of various laws and regulations. It is probably because they know that the reasoning is weak. What is strange is that our government does not care about these more than 3 million Overseas Chinese. Since the late Qing Dynasty for hundreds of years, it has not established diplomatic relations with Siam, allowing the Siamese government to unilaterally approve and implement the exclusion policy. It is a rare phenomenon in the world. On the government side, or because our country has informally proposed to the Siamese government to conclude a treaty of diplomatic relations, the government ignores it, so it has not been implemented. In fact, China and Siam should not only have such a large

Overseas Chinese Issue Should seek a proper solution, that is, to discuss the trade between the two countries, at a minimum, there must be a commercial treaty concluded, because the Siamese government regards rice production as a major demonstration, accounting for 50% of the total export goods, and the number imported into our country is the largest. According to the statistical report of the Siamese government's Ministry of Commerce, in 1933, Siamese rice imported into China and Hong Kong accounted for more than 60% of its total exports, and in 1934, imports into China and Hong Kong also accounted for 34% of its total exports. Siamese rice actually regards our country as its largest sales market. Recently, the Dutch East Indies, Malaya, and other places have increased import taxes or restricted imports, followed by Japan, which will also control the import of foreign rice. Siamese rice has been greatly hit, so now

Siamese Rice Sales Have to rely on our country as its last resort, that is, the general public opinion in Siam and the insightful people in the government and the opposition also advocate concluding a commercial treaty with our country. If China can use this point to demand the conclusion of a Sino-Siamese treaty, it is not impossible to achieve the goal. In short, the Siamese government's exclusion of Overseas Chinese has reached the most serious period. If our government still delays, it will not only make 2 million Overseas Chinese gradually become aliens, but also make other countries follow suit. How will it be able to stand in the world? All compatriots in the country should pay attention to it. Reported by Xu Shiying of the Relief Committee

Du Yuesheng and Others Raise Funds for Disaster Relief and Receive the Jade Award from the National Government 125

Reported by Xu Shiying of the Relief Committee; Chu Minyi, Representative of the Executive Yuan, Conferred the Award

According to the Central News Agency, the Executive Yuan previously presented a petition from the Relief Affairs Committee to award medals to disaster relief personnel.
