Free Talk

Further Discussion on Ballad Novels 202

— Hanfeng

After writing "A Discussion on Ballad Novels," I obtained Li Boyuan's "Gengzi National Crisis Ballad." Its preface quotes the first paragraph, saying: "Reading the Legend of the Palace of Eternal Life, when Li Guinian narrates the lost tales of the Kaiyuan era, it is impassioned, generous, and thoroughly vivid. Reading also the Legend of the Peach Blossom Fan, when Liu Jingting and Su Kunshang recount the Yangzhou soldiers' mutiny, it is poignantly heart-wrenching, and filled with sorrow and indignation. Because of their extensive and profound writing, with words and tongue both employed, they could recite and sing from afar, tears accompanying their voices. The power of ballad novels to move people deeply and extensively, through the excellence of performers, is evident here. Therefore, the value of ballad novels truly extends beyond what ordinary ballad writers say, which is merely 'to dispel sorrow and pass the time,' and it certainly has its significance."

Ballads and drum ballads have somewhat similar forms. Generally, in the north, the distinction is simple: if accompanied by drums, it's a drum ballad; if accompanied by the three-stringed lute, it's a ballad. Southern ballads, although influenced by drum ballads, incorporate a greater element of folk songs and tunes. Like opera, ballads also have northern and southern styles. Not only that, but they can also be divided into Kunqu, Gaoqiang, Luan Tan, Bangziqiang, Shipaiqiang, Huangqiang, Xianziqiang, Juanqiang, Luoluoqiang, Zhouguziqiang, and so on. These divisions are naturally determined by regional differences. For example, Shipaiqiang is popular in Jiangnan, Huangqiang in Shaanxi, Xianziqiang is prevalent in Zhili, Juanqiang and Luoluoqiang flourish in Henan, and Zhouguziqiang is found in Shandong. These vary by location and cannot be fully listed.

Regarding the organization of chapters, the most complex include several forms: poetry, lyrics, eulogies, suites, and "pianzi," with "pianzi" being the main component. The so-called "pianzi" refers to the sung sections within the chapter. Each section is called a "pianzi," and the number of "pianzi" in each chapter is not fixed. Poetry and lyrics are mostly used for the opening of each chapter or the ending of the entire book. Most writers typically quote works from predecessors, distinguishing between those directly related to the plot and those of general reference. The former often involves original creations, while the latter is gleaned from readily available old texts. Eulogies and suites are added to specific sections based on factual needs, such as the "Moling Autumn" suite at the end of "The Swallow Letter Ballad." Of course, works of other forms can be added at any time, such as the small songs in "The Tale of the Double Jade Cups," the imperial edict in "The Tale of the Double Jade Swallows," and the proclamation in "The Swallow Letter." However, these can be considered exceptions. The number of characters per line in the "pianzi" is mostly seven or ten, with other lengths determined by the necessities of the content, without much restriction.

The writing technique for "pianzi" prioritizes natural rhymes. Another crucial element that significantly contributes to the success of ballads is the lively application of idioms, slang, and popular vernacular, which can make the "pianzi" more vivid and powerful. For example, "Compared to you, he's afraid the cantaloupe is too sweet to eat. Pity him, how can he swallow the unspeakable bitterness?" This usage is so natural and interesting. Secondly, the application of humor is also necessary, as it can refresh the audience's tired spirits. To summarize the principle: the success of a suite depends entirely on applying effort to the eight words: "accessible and easily understood, lively and elegant."

Due to the freedom of form and the flexible use of rhymed vernacular, ballad novels have advantages beyond "describing fine details of things and trivial emotions with utmost care." This format retains the strengths of verse while incorporating prose, developing descriptive narratives that vividly paint scenes with sound and imagery. At the same time, it practically breaks the traditional notion that vernacular and colloquial language cannot be used in writing, proving that when used appropriately, it not only does no harm but also makes the writing more lively and gives readers and listeners a vivid impression.

Attached: Dan Yuan Discusses Four Taboos and Six Necessities for Storytelling

"The first taboo is to widely invite respected and influential guests. The second taboo is to casually discuss lottery tickets and divination slips with fellow villagers. The third taboo is that a blind man can never sing in tune. The fourth taboo is that the host may not understand the silk strings. The necessities are: a clean ground paved with stone and brick. The necessity is: a refreshing and sunny day, cool in summer and warm in winter. The necessity is: a large teacup to quench thirst and promote saliva. The necessity is: a small incense plate for smoking and lighting fire. The necessity is: a boy quickly setting the table. The necessity is: a servant first securing the benches. And then, the sounds of the lute are as bright as snow. The words are spoken, each one rounder than a pearl."

On Poetry and Music 203

— Chen Junhan

The most important difference between poetry and prose lies in that poetry should have musical rhythm, musical melody, and musical emotion; whereas prose does not.

I recall having previously discussed the uniqueness of language in poetry and thoughts suitable for poetry, as well as the unity of content and form in poetry. Now, let's further discuss the importance of poetry and music.

If poetry lacks the elements of music, it can hardly be considered poetry.

My friend, Ye Jun, brought his poems for me to read. Recently, I also read "Escaping Famine," which he was pleased with. He is indeed someone with great interest in poetry, and he wishes to become a poet himself. Yes, I read his poems with great enthusiasm. However, after reading, I cannot deny that he merely presented the suffering of refugees in the countryside and their escape to the city as factual narratives, written in lines like a poetic form on paper. The direct impression it gave me was that it was no different from a piece of prose. There was nothing else beyond that. Furthermore, the poem lacked emotional components.

"Poetry is music that expresses emotion through words," I said.

If we were to take this as a definition of poetry, it would naturally be biased and incomplete. However, compared to prose, poetry contains the important element of music.

Now, allow me to cite some examples to illustrate the differences between poetry and prose:

"A carpenter might say to his plane:

'Plane, now I will use you to smooth the wood.'

But Carson's poem writes:

'O plane, shave swiftly,

Singing on the workbench;

The board heats up like a copper comb,

Wood shavings flow in torrents.'

Is there a difference between the carpenter's words and Carson's poem?

The difference is significant, even though the subject matter is the same.

The carpenter's words are simply an invitation for the plane to work, while in Carson's poem, we hear the sound of the plane smoothing the wood, and Carson conveys the joy of labor, the poetic sense of labor, and the music of labor.

Therefore, the difference between poetry and prose lies in the fact that poetry has musical rhythm, musical melody, and musical emotion, and it is realistic."

Some poems have rhymes at the end of each line; however, some poems do not have rhymes, but the descriptive phrases still have musical rhythm and harmony.

Mad Woman 204

— Shen Shengshi

This girl, her heart pierced by deep sorrow, went mad.

A mad person reverts to innocence; her expression of pain is so distressing!

At the beginning of the summer vacation, her parents sent her from the hospital to the art school.

For the first few days of class, she was so gentle and intelligent; we didn't know she was mad.

After two weeks, her unfortunate symptoms gradually began to appear.

One afternoon, we saw her dancing the foxtrot alone on the walkway. Many classmates went to watch her; she showed no embarrassment at all.

After that, she stopped attending classes on her own and often played the piano alone in the music room. Accompanied by the tinkling of the piano, she sang Beethoven's mournful tunes in her trembling, hoarse voice, carrying the songs from the gauze window to a lake of slightly green spring water.

Through the wall, we heard her laughing wildly for no reason, laughing so long and so bitterly. Finally, we heard her collapse onto the keyboard and cry!

She was intelligent and beautiful; she had a talent for music and could speak English fluently.

We saw her speaking fluent English to the wall by herself. On another occasion, she embraced a thick osmanthus tree in the corridor and kissed it wildly.

However, we didn't understand the reason for her madness until after she was expelled from the school. Her tragedy then spread throughout the school!

It was said that her fiancé was an American student. When he returned home after completing his studies, like a bolt from the blue, he suddenly died of an acute illness on the ship.

This profound shock shattered her heart; this incurable disease was beyond medical help!

I left the art school three years ago. When I think about that long period of painful struggle, the good dreams of those days, like a thin spring drizzle, vanished. Since then, I have been lonely, letting life drag on my feet, not looking up as I hurry along.

God! Protect my iron heart; don't let me go mad!

Fog 205

— Liu Bing

The dawn on the equator is silent and gentle. However, almost every morning, when we open the window and look out, we find that we are surrounded by a misty white fog. In front of us is a vast expanse of white; we can't see anything clearly. The scene before our eyes is like an overexposed photograph.

The morning fog obscures everything, masking the true appearance of everything on the equator. However, in this hazy atmosphere, I opened my eyes, and I saw through this misty veil. I saw the unvarnished truth:

The rows of rubber trees, in the past, boasted of their value, but now, I see them forcing a smile as they support their heavily wounded bodies. For decades, they have provided exploitation for people. Now, their blood has run dry, their essence has been exhausted, like a critically ill old man, discarded by people as worthless…

I also saw that mountain shining with fiery light. In the past, it was a treasure trove of gold, and many people lived prosperous lives because of it. But now, the mine is desolate, and the cranes on the hillside have long been unattended, leaving only iron skeletons rusting.

In the city, you see those speeding trucks, carrying wealthy men and women. But if you look closely at their faces, their eyes are covered with a shadowy gloom. Their laughter hides glistening tears; they lament their own decline…

The heavy morning fog obscures all of this; people cannot see the truth. The entire equatorial line (perhaps the whole world) is shrouded in fog, causing people to be in a daze.

I imagine everything at the window. I looked at the eastern horizon. When will the golden threads of sunlight break through this dense fog?

Rainbow Clouds 206

— Feng Zikai

This happened last summer.

It hadn't rained for two months. The sun shone for fifteen hours every day. The mercury in the thermometer climbed above one hundred degrees every day. The bottom of the river was exposed everywhere. Ponds became depressions. Weeds turned yellow and stood erect in the gray-white dry soil. The heat's misery and the drought's panic filled everything.

There was no place in the room that wasn't hot. Sitting on a stool felt like sitting on a copper stove. Touching the table felt like touching a chimney. The wax candles bent down from the candlesticks, curving into the shape of a magnet. Mints, left on the table for a while, twisted open and dissolved completely, evaporating. The dog lay panting under the table with its tongue hanging out; people occupied every doorway and fanned themselves tirelessly. Their wrists ached from fanning, and sweat poured out incessantly. Although there was a lot of sweat, drinking water became a problem. Water carried from afar cost four coppers a load, and poured into the water tank, it looked like milk. Water carried from nearby cost ten copper coins a load, and after settling, half a load was mud. Families that could afford to buy water used it sparingly. Water used to wash faces was saved for washing clothes, water used to wash clothes was saved for washing pants, and water used to wash pants was saved for watering flowers. Families that couldn't afford to buy water had small-footed mothers and children of several years old carrying buckets to fetch water from afar. Every day, they worried about the heat, worried about the water, and worried about the drought to come. Fields that were tilled late hadn't been planted yet. The soil had hardened like stone. Seedlings in fields that were tilled early had grown, but they had all turned into withered grass. The entire village was mobilized to tread water. First, they tread water from the big river into the small river, then from the small river into the port and canals, and finally from the port and canals into the fields. But working fifteen hours a day, the water people treaded in wasn't enough to compensate for the evaporation from the sun shining for fifteen hours a day. Today there was news that the crops in the southwest corner had all turned yellow; tomorrow there would be more news that the waterwheels on the canal banks had increased to eight hundred and some. When people met, they initially did nothing but lament helplessly: "What can we do if it just doesn't rain?" "The heavens have completely forgotten about rain!" But later they reached a conclusion, and everyone anxiously told each other when they met: "If it doesn't rain in ten more days, a great famine is coming!"

In the following ten days, everyone was too busy to worry about the heat, staring intently at the sky, hoping for rain. Every morning when they woke up, the first thing they did was ask about the weather, but the weather was just sunny, sunny, sunny… sunny for ten days straight. After the tenth day, it was still sunny, sunny, sunny… sunny for countless days. Some people said despairingly: "Even if it rains right now, it's already too late." But most people still didn't despair: farmers still desperately treaded water, and even the elderly and children came out to participate. The people in the town still looked up at the sky every day, hoping it would rain immediately, or that there would still be a last-minute remedy. The reason they didn't despair was that for more than ten days, there had been a few rainbow clouds hanging in the southeast corner, floating and sinking, sometimes large, sometimes small, sometimes bright, sometimes dim, showing people all sorts of signs that it was about to rain, maintaining a glimmer of hope for them. Sometimes they rose up, grew bigger, darkened, and seemed to say bravely to the people treading water and watching the sky: "Don't despair! We're bringing rain!" So the people treading water increased their courage and treaded even more desperately; the people watching the sky gained hope, happily showing joy and cheering each other: "It's going to rain! It's going to rain!" The elderly shook their hands to stop them: "Don't shout, don't shout, you'll scare it away!" Soon those rainbow clouds were indeed scared away. They gradually sank under the scorching sun, became smaller, faded, dispersed, and finally hid below the horizon. People were happy for nothing and still returned to the heat's misery and the drought's panic. There was a moment of empty joy every day, but every day they couldn't escape the misery and terror. Originally, these rainbow clouds were just hanging there for people to look at, emptily giving people comfort and encouragement. Later, people saw through them. No matter how colorful and dazzling they were, floating in the sky, they just lowered their heads and struggled with the heat and drought, living day by day, no longer falling for those empty rainbow clouds.

This happened last summer. Eventually, it did rain, but it was no use, and the great famine finally arrived. Now, farmers are eating chaff, workers are idle with their tools, and merchants are guarding empty counters, all waiting for the silkworms to mature and the wheat to ripen, no longer recalling the past.

Why am I bringing up old events here now? I once painted a picture of these rainbow clouds during the drought. Now, I've selected sixty paintings depicting the people's livelihood from the paintings I've made since the drought and compiled them into a book. I've put this painting of the rainbow clouds at the beginning and named the book "Rainbow Clouds." This is not just imitating the "Guan Ju" and "Ge Tan," taking the first line as the title. Because I feel that the people's livelihood today is always filled with the heat's misery and the drought's panic, and there are also a few rainbow clouds always hanging before our eyes, constantly comforting us with beautiful forms, encouraging us, and maintaining a glimmer of hope for our future, no different from the situation last summer. So I'm recording this situation as the preface to this book.

After finishing the record, I began to have doubts: Can these rainbow clouds of mine not just be for people to appreciate emptily, emptily to comfort and encourage people? Can they satisfy the longing of the drought era? I know they can't. Because the rainbow clouds depicted here are too small and too few. How can just these few cause abundant rain? I'm afraid they will just be there for people to appreciate emptily and then sink below the horizon.

Three Days (2) 207

— Luo Hong

But Youcai didn't even glance at his brother. He just lowered his head and rubbed his bare feet on the ground. After a while, the big toe on his right foot lifted up more than half an inch, like a son, forcefully clamping the calf of the other foot. Only after Youfa finished speaking did he raise his head and stare at his brother in the doorway, saying:

"You always say these things, I'm tired of hearing them! Being a wet nurse can naturally earn some money, but I won't go to Mr. Lu's. We have to borrow money from him, paying two percent interest per month. Why do we have to have the daughter-in-law be a wet nurse before he's willing to lend it? He wants his own son to be well, don't I want my own son to be well? I definitely won't agree. I don't want to have the child taken to someone else's house, becoming pitifully thin like a monkey!"

"I don't think they're being that heartless. They don't like the wet nurse they're using. Her milk is sparse. Your daughter-in-law is young and has a lot of milk. Of course they like her. We just happen to need to borrow money from them, and they're afraid we won't agree, so they want us to agree first." Youfa's eyes darted, sometimes fixed on the ground, sometimes fixed on Youcai's face, as if regretting that he had said too much.

"What do you know? They're the most ruthless. He seems to think two percent interest is too little, deliberately trying to make things difficult for us. I just won't put up with it!"

Youcai raised his voice, and seeing that his brother didn't respond, he said:

"You're afraid of Mr. Lu's shadow as soon as you see it. You're more than ten years older than me, but you have the courage of a sesame seed. What's there to be afraid of? The more you're afraid of them, the more unrestrained they become. I see through them now."

"See through them? I don't believe you see through them. You've become like this because you listened to Hu Yongliang's nonsense." The older brother seemed a little angry, his eyes, filled with red veins, staring hard at Youcai's face, as if asking: "Can you deny my discovery?" After a moment, he lowered his voice and said, "Youcai, don't go learning from Hu Yongliang. That kid has lived in the city for two years, and he looks down on everyone. I don't think he'll have a good outcome. Don't learn from him."

Youcai didn't speak. On his face, tanned the color of soy sauce by the sun, his cheekbones twitched. At this moment, the child in the firewood corner of the room suddenly cried. This clear cry broke through the melancholy silence, and both men breathed a sigh of relief. A woman with a round, dark face walked over from the stove in the next room, picked up the child, and quickly walked away.

"Agree to it, Youcai. Stop saying those resentful words. We poor people can't be like that!" Youfa changed his tone to a gentler one, walked to the table, and picked up a water pipe, as if he wanted to talk with Youcai for half a day.

"Don't say these empty words. I'm just telling you, it won't work if she leaves the house. With both of us busy working in the fields, who will do the cooking? Last year, Sister-in-law went to the city to work. You yourself said that Agen's mother couldn't go, and it was useful to have a woman at home. Now you're saying this again. It's really—"

Shen Bao Local Supplement

Random Thoughts

Rewarding Marriage and Competitive Childbearing 208

— Jiawei

"Cultivate blessings and longevity, many sons and grandsons," this was originally a common saying—no, a "mantra"—in our ancient feudal society! From the mouths of relatives and friends when offering birthday greetings and congratulations, down to the mouths of beggars begging for alms, they all used it.

Indeed, since "the European wind gradually spread east," especially since the "May Fourth Movement," our society has become somewhat "reformed." At the same time, perhaps because of the poor economic conditions and social unrest of today, the lives of many, many people have gradually become difficult, causing panic and forcing them to struggle on the front lines of hunger, cold, and life and death. Thus, this "auspicious saying" of "cultivate blessings and longevity, many sons and grandsons" seems to be threatened today and is no longer sufficiently "universally applicable," right?

As for the "civilized countries" of Western Europe, they are certainly much more "enlightened" than we are. Therefore, there is no doubt that these feudal ideas have long been eradicated, right? Moreover, at present, this group of capitalist imperialist countries is reaching the extreme peak of "panic"; "the power of monopoly is expanding day by day, and the unemployment panic and conflicting contradictions are expanding day by day." So, "many sons and grandsons" are also facing difficulties and threats for them, right?

However, the reality is quite the opposite. Please see the reports in various newspapers the other day about the National Society of Rome: "Italy has become a honeymoon country today, with more than two thousand newly married couples being provided with expenses by the Fascist Party to enjoy their holidays together. Each newly married couple can receive five hundred lire; this is part of the government's marriage promotion plan." Also, Reuters reported: "Yesterday, a total of two thousand three hundred and fifty-three couples held wedding ceremonies in Rome, following the Fascist slogan of 'early marriage' and 'large families.' Most of the new couples are under twenty-five years old, and some are only sixteen years old."

Look! "Early marriage," "large families," "only sixteen years old," "two thousand three hundred and fifty-three couples," truly "mighty," "unprecedented," but for what purpose—"to have noble sons early"!

I remember reading a statistic in the newspaper last month: "According to statistics from the National Socialist Party's Racial Department, Germany's marriage rate in 1934 still holds the record unmatched by any other country. In the first half of the year, there were 334,600 marriages in Germany, an increase of 32 percent compared to the same period in 1933. Germany also ranks first in terms of fertility. Last year, a total of 576,800 people were born. Furthermore, the labor front's newspaper, the 'German People's Daily,' commented that the competition to increase the population must continue, and families with many children should be subsidized."

However, their so-called "encouragement of marriage" and "the competition to increase the population must continue" is not for the sake of "cultivating blessings and longevity"! If we pay attention to the news that various countries are advocating today, such as "rearming," "increasing the national defense budget," "building new ships," "war clouds are tightening, and countries are hoarding wheat," it is not difficult to understand: what kind of role are these "plans" and "records" playing—very simple! They are being processed and competitively manufactured into "cannon fodder" for the Second Great Massacre!

After Becoming Deaf 209

— Ruomu

The city at night opens its bright eyes, its flickering lights illuminating its malnourished and bloodless face, wrinkled with countless lines, making it weaker and more sallow, like faded yellow paper, dimly lit without a trace of light.

On the road, on the night road in the bustling city, the noisy sounds resonate in every corner. To the people living lavishly in this city, these clamorous sounds are like playing happy songs, captivating their hearts. But he, like someone abandoned by the people of this world, does not enjoy these sounds at all, because his hearing is numb, he is deaf. He no longer has the fortune to hear the musical sounds of the city.

He himself also felt inexplicable. Since becoming deaf, he has been envying those who feel happy listening to music. A year ago, when his hearing was still very sharp, he hated the noisy sounds of the city attacking him, sometimes making his uneasy heart even more agitated. He always hoped to escape this city and go to a quiet place. But this kind of thought was an impossible fantasy for him. If he left the city, he would suffer even more pain. The pressure of life forced him to live here. But since he became deaf, this attitude has completely changed. At first, he envied others, but recently he has gradually become resentful. In his heart, a hostile idea emerged. He thought that those who were not deaf were too undeserving, too overbearing towards those who had lost their hearing. It seemed that those who were not deaf, in his opinion, should not exist in this world.

Because of his loss of hearing, his heart became quiet and lonely. However, chaotic thoughts became even more agitated in his heart. This unbearable situation in front of him made him feel more pain when he thought quietly.

He, a forty-year-old man, lost his job because of his deafness, which made his life even more unbearable. Although he had no wife or children, his parents, who were in their seventies, were like a very heavy burden pressing on his shoulders, which had lost their ability to bear weight. It is extremely difficult for a deaf person to struggle alone in the world, but asking him to take on this burden again would crush him to death.

He couldn't help but think of his teaching life before he became deaf. Although he didn't live a very prosperous life at that time, he didn't fall into such a desolate poverty after losing his job. Yes, when he had a job, he was often dissatisfied with his life and hoped for new developments, but that kind of hope would not be realized. On the contrary, now that he has fallen into such an environment, comparing the two lives, he naturally felt that his past life was happy and fulfilling.

"After teaching for so many years, now I'm unemployed and have become deaf."

He often sighed like this, and often had a thought of being tired of the world. He knew that his hope was over. But when he came back from outside and saw the bitter faces of his parents in their seventies struggling on the line of starvation, he had an idea of repaying their nurturing kindness. That kind of thought of taking his own life gradually faded and disappeared in his heart. But the question of "how to live" in front of him made his heart beat faster.

"How to live?" This difficult question was like a thousand-pound stone pressing tightly on his heart. This deaf and unemployed teacher was troubled by this question all day long. All the struggles made him despair and feel the insignificance of life.

Silent Yearning 210

— Simon

A pair of eyes that secretly held the passionate emotions of a precocious girl, a unique taste of the South! A Guangdong product, just thinking about it, my heart was captivated by that pair of passionate eyes, dark and round, like longan seeds in summer, emitting piercing red light.

Oh, Luciana, the goddess of love in the heart of my lover!

That day was a troublesome spring afternoon that easily made people dream. Spring is a very suitable season for love. Just as I was about to take a nap, a woman's sharp voice suddenly called out outside the house.

I listened quietly: strangely familiar, could it be Luciana!

Sure enough, Luciana appeared at the door, dressed up and smiling charmingly.

I really jumped up. Luciana was very pretty today: healthy, fair, and rosy complexion, strong arms, full breasts, and her trousers were rolled up high to her knees. The beauty of her thighs was wonderfully condensed in my eyes.

Oh, Luciana, passionate yet with a Western-style vigor!

—Luciana, what's the matter?

—It's spring, let's go horseback riding in the suburbs and spend a boring afternoon.

My drowsy spirit suddenly burst with energy.

The spring fields lay under the gentle spring sunshine, serenely beautiful. The sky was orange-blue, and the clouds were also orange-blue, drifting low above our heads. In the fields, green rapeseed flowers were interspersed with white rapeseed flowers, and the fragrance of green and white rapeseed flowers mixed with the scent of mud wafted in the breeze.

The breeze caressed Luciana's curly hair, and her bangs fluttered.

Spring is really a season for love! Everything was intoxicating. I felt happy. Joyful.

On the road, we sat on horseback, facing the warm wind, moving forward slowly. Luciana gently whistled a popular tune, and I followed along. When we reached the path, I let Luciana run ahead, without any hesitation, like a brave empress, but my heart was fragile.

Do I have a share of love for her, I suddenly asked myself secretly.

Passing through a pond path with tall reeds, Luciana used her hand to move away the obstructing reed branches, and the sharp leaves pricked her thumb, drawing a little blood, but she seemed not to want me to know, and quietly took out a small handkerchief to wipe it, but I saw it clearly.

—Luciana, why is your hand bleeding?

—Nothing, just a little sting.

Luciana turned her head and smiled charmingly, but my heart couldn't help but feel sad.

That red blood is the symbol of love, the symbol of a young girl's passionate youth!

Towards evening, we returned with a bit of fatigue.

A troublesome spring afternoon passed by in such a gentle mood.

It was the first time I played with Luciana.

Luciana has a pair of eyes that secretly hold the passionate emotions of a precocious girl, a symbol of love! When she smiles, it's like a blooming rose, making one think of her bright young body and her bright young youth.

I can hardly forget her for a moment, but I also

Page 23

Quietly sediment my young yearning for love, my young silent tenderness, in the depths of my heart, without telling anyone, not even Luciana. But I know that she is smart and sensible, and I know that she also has a young heart of love and yearning like myself, with silent tenderness sedimented in the depths of her heart. Just like myself.—Luciana, when will you let our two silent hearts of love and longing bloom together, tell me!

Another Year, Spring Flowers Fall 211

— Luo Jia

My garden, even though it hasn't become so barren that there isn't a single flower: nevertheless, the pansies huddled in the corner of the wall, the sparse morning glory vines twining around the hibiscus hedge, the maiden-like shy mimosa, and the rustic ten-foot red, they all bloom with some lonely flowers, even the green of the leaves is lonely, like my own mood. They make my garden seem too lonely! I believe that without those flowers, my garden should still have some spring spirit!

There's no need (or maybe I don't want to) rush around the enclosure looking for traces of spring, I plan like this. I know that my current portion of loneliness is a suitable punishment for the excitement and liveliness of the past (to put it lightly, it's an adjustment!). And I am content with this kind of punishment, gladly.

The hazy twilight, like a misty valley, embraces my night garden. Will the night garden be even more lonely? So I took my wisteria cane (I'm a young old man!), stepped into the night garden, and the faint, botanical fragrance generously provided me with gentle breaths. My nerves were a little sharper, so I wanted to open my eyes and prepare to search for something in the twilight garden? Regardless of whether what I found was what I loved. However, what could I get? The dancing posture of the flower branches in the twilight? The evening breeze rippling with the breath of spring?

In the serene thoughts, I don't hope to get anything? Nor do I hope not to get anything? I stubbornly hold on to my past whisper:

"Gain and loss disturb the serene thoughts, this is a cruel act."

So, I closed my eyes. In the lonely veil of the twilight garden, I had a pool of quiet contemplation.

(I said: My contemplation is wasteful, wasted in the weight of memories, floating like a dream, like a yellow leaf, gently blown by the sentimental wind, falling into the sea of thin sorrow, and the lonely twilight garden will be stained with a layer of melancholic color, this is obviously too stupid! Too stupid.)

I cleverly stretched my hand into my pocket, and a cigarette was placed in my white coat. The faint light of the match flashed, but it broke through the silence of the garden. A pair of plum finches roosting on the apricot tree, perhaps not used to the light, flew up and chirped. This, for me, was very unsettling, and at the same time, it was like the gardener's eviction notice. So, I quietly went out!

As usual, every twilight, my feet will step into the garden. I am willing to do so, and weariness cannot take away my hobby.

Today's twilight had a faint moonlight. When I stepped into the garden as usual, closed my eyes and sat quietly, and when I had sat long enough and opened my eyes, preparing to leave this garden, I found some fallen petals, lying there lonely. So, I felt a sense of sorrow for no reason. My emotions are so fragile!

Yes, the flowers in the garden make the garden seem a little more lonely, but I am not used to the weaving of things. I like the ordinary, the normal. I can't bear to see what has been added to my garden? Likewise, I can't bear to see what is missing from my garden? (Because I love the tranquility of my heart, and the tranquility of my heart will be plundered by the changes in things.)

Because of this, I and my garden will suddenly become estranged! The small stone path in front of the garden gate, full of blue bitterness, no longer has my footprints! I have made up my mind like this.

Next year when the flowers bloom, will I still be living here? I dare not think about it.

Movie News

Random Notes on "The Constant Nymph" 214

— Yunmen

"The Constant Nymph", currently showing in Nanjing, was originally named "Vanessa Her Love Story". Vanessai Her Love Story is one of the four masterpieces of the famous British novelist Hugh Walpole, who specializes in writing about the Herries family of Cumberland, England. When MGM decided to use his work as a script, Walpole himself went to Hollywood to supervise and assist. After the film was completed and became famous, he returned to his home country.

In "The Constant Nymph", of course, the acting talents of the two leading actors, Helen Hayes and Robert Montgomery, are beyond introduction; but Hayes deeply hates the life under the spotlight, so she forbids her own daughter from following in her footsteps. Her only hope in the future is to be a proactive director. At the same time, Montgomery plans to retire and own thousands of acres of fertile land, living the life of a farmer. Agnes Anderson, who made her screen debut as Montgomery's wife, is also a selected standard beauty.

We know that Queen Victoria was the first Empress of India to merge India. She held her Golden Jubilee ceremony in June 1887, and "The Constant Nymph" also features a performance about this grand and solemn ceremony: what is especially rare is that the background, costumes, fashion, etc., are very similar to the real thing.

Several more points are worth noting here: (1) The producer of this film is David O. Selznick, who has contributed to blockbusters such as "David Copperfield", "Viva Villa!", "Little Women", and "Dinner at Eight"; (2) The director is William K. Howard, famous for directing "The Cat and the Fiddle"; (3) Supporting stars include Myrna Loy, Louis Stone, and Otto Kruger. These can guarantee that "The Constant Nymph" is indeed a romantic work that is extraordinary.

Celebrity News 215

Mingxing Film Company is moving, which is quite busy. It is said that they will all move into the new address on Fenglin Bridge in the next few days.

There is a song called "National Soul Song" in "National Soul", which is very beautiful. Yesterday, Gong Jianong, Zhao Dan, Yan Gongshang, Sun Min, and Li Qing practiced in the Mingxing drama department and sang very enthusiastically.

Shen Xiling will finish his "Boat Girl" in the next few days, so there are his sets on the Mingxing studio every day.

Xu Xinfu's newly compiled "Jade Horse" has passed the preliminary review. On the 30th, the cast was called together in the Mingxing director department to lecture on the plot. The main characters in the film are Wang Zhengxin, Gong Jianong, Yan Yuexian, Zhao Dan, and Gu Lanjun.

The second issue of Mingxing Bi-Monthly has been published on schedule. It is expected that the sales will be more than the first issue because the content is more exciting than the first issue.

The Lianyou Film Association has been quite active since its internal reorganization. The original members who have re-registered and those who have heard the news and went to register are extremely enthusiastic because the association's purpose is pure, so it is very developed.

Wu Lizhu Galloping in the Suburbs 216

Most celebrities in the capital live an enjoyable life, but martial arts star Wu Lizhu is different. She does not go to dance halls but likes to ride horses and drive cars. These days, the weather is mild and full of spring, so she drives to Longhua, Zhenru, and Wusong to fully enjoy the natural beauty.

Sky Burial in Tibet 217

Tibet has a strange custom called sky burial, which is that after a person dies, their skin is peeled off, and then the flesh is scraped off, mashed together, and the bones are also crushed, mixed together, and let the divine vulture fly over to eat them. The crew of Yueming Film Company completely captured this tragic scene on camera. According to Wang Hanxiong, after he finished shooting at that time, he couldn't eat anything all day.

Secret Screening of "Mad Marriage" 218

Yueming Film Company's first all-dialogue sound film "Mad Marriage" has now been completed. A secret screening was held at the Central Grand Theatre on Six Horses Road at 11:00 PM the night before. All attendees were company colleagues. It lasted until 1:30 AM. As a result, except for some minor changes to the editing, the photography and sound recording were unanimously considered satisfactory.

Yuan Meiyun Gets Married 219

A reporter visited Yihua Film Company to see Yuan Congmei's sound film "Storm" and saw the lead actress Yuan Meiyun. After some small talk, the reporter asked Yuan if she had ever been married. At that time, everyone in the studio focused their eyes on Yuan Meiyun, secretly guessing that a blush of shyness must appear on her face, but unexpectedly, she did not show any shyness at all and answered very generously, "I am already married." "Already married?" the reporter asked in surprise, "When, where, and to whom did you get married?"

Everyone in the studio looked strangely surprised.

"I got married once with Wang Yin in Shi Dongshan's film 'The Beginning of Man'."

"Hahahaha!" A burst of laughter erupted in the studio.
